  746. e.l.f. offers quite a few good products and this is one of them. Countless makeup reviewers, makeup artists, and regular people who make makeup tutorials on YouTube swear by this primer even when most of their other cosmetics are high end.<br /><br />I really enjoyed this primer. I'm still learning how to correctly apply it so I don't use more than necessary. But it goes on very smooth. It slides across your fingers and face like the most slippery lubricant you can imagine. At the same time, the texture of it is SOOO soft and silky. It actually feels great just rubbing it between thumb and forefinger. It's a pleasant experience!<br /><br />The only problem I have with this product, and why I gave it 4 stars instead of 5, is that there is so little -actual- product in this pump. It looks, by its size, like there is a lot more product inside it. When I started running out, exceptionally soon, I unscrewed the housing and took the pump out and looked inside. The actual well that holds the product is TINY! I mean very tiny. And there's still a bit of product on the sides of the well which can't be drawn up into the pump for some reason. I'm having to take it apart and scoop out what I need with a toothpick.<br /><br />Speaking of toothpicks, I just had an idea. I took the bottle apart so that I could get an -approximate- measurement for the inside of that little well. When I put the toothpick in, and it hit the bottom, MOST of the toothpick was still above the rim. Probably 2/3rds of it. I marked the toothpick and measured it. The well, from the bottom to the top of the mouth of it where the other bits screw onto it, it's exactly 1 inch. 1 inch deep. The diameter is less than 2 cm wide which is a little less than 3/4 of an inch. So, yeah, teensy!<br /><br />If this was one of e.l.f.'s $1 - $3 products, I'd have absolutely no problem with that. But for $6, you should get a little more product. At least that's MY opinion.<br /><br />So, in summary, it's a great product and will probably work for most skin types and blend well with most foundations (though I'm not sure if it would work well under powder foundation). However, the small amount of product you get might not be work the $6 price tag depending on how you use it and what you're looking for. Hope this helps. =)nd will probably work for most skin types and blend well with most foundations (though I'm not sure if it would work well under powder foundation). The packaging makes it look like it's a more fancy/expensive product (thought the plastic FEELS cheap). But trying to get the product out can be a pain. The pump seems very cheap. It never wanted to come out and when it finally did, it spurted out very little at a time (which was annoying). I have the bottle sitting in front of me as I'm typing this, trying to pump a drop onto my finger, and it doesn't work at all. I took it apart and noticed that on the pump, there's no tube going down the center of the bottle to actually GET the product up and out of the bottle. It's just a little stub. So once you've used it enough for it to go down about 1/2 of an inch, the rest won't come out anymore. That's just lame.<br /><br />Now let me try and explain the weird texture of this stuff... When I say weird, I definitely mean weird. Visually it looks like a gel, but it feels much lighter and softer, almost silky. I stopped using it for a while and my skin cleared up. Then I tried it again (just to be sure) and again, red skin.<br /><br />To sum it all up, I don't like this at all. If for some weird reason I needed primer for my fingers or hands then it feels great! But definitely not my face. We all have different skin, what may work for me might not work for someone else. All I can recommend is that you give it a try. It's not a whole lot of money out of the pocket, and it's worth a shot before you commit to buying something much more expensive.
